GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING SERVICES

ENGIE PUAKO SOLAR DEVELOPMENT 
PUAKO, SOUTH KOHALA, HAWAII 
W.O. 8098-10     FEBRUARY 24, 2021 
SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS 
A new solar farm project is proposed on vacant land encompassing an area of over 
400 acres in the Puako area on the Island of Hawaii. We understand that wide flange 
beams (W6x9) are considered for the foundation support of the new solar arrays for the 
project. Therefore, a test pile program consisting of installing and testing W6x9 wide 
flange beams was undertaken to provide pile driving and load testing data for the design 
of the production pile foundation system. 
A total of 128 W6x9 test piles were installed across the project site. Refusal 
conditions were encountered in 28 of the 115 piles driven directly into the existing ground 
surface.  Therefore, 13 additional piles were driven into 5- and 6-inch diameter predrilled 
holes (backfilled with base course prior to pile driving) to evaluate alternate pile foundation 
design when refusal conditions are encountered during the driven pile installation.  Based 
on the results of the pile load testing, predrilling using a 5-inch diameter bit produced more 
favorable results than using a 6-inch diameter bit for the W6x9 piles. 
In general, passing results were obtained for the vast majority of compressive 
(111 out of 112) and lateral (112 out of 117) load tests performed for the project.  However, 
about 20 percent of the piles tested (23 out of 115) failed in tension.  Therefore, load tests 
should be performed on production piles to confirm the design load capacities.  Contingency 
measures to handle the piles that failed the load tests should be developed for the 
production pile installation. 
The text of this report should be referred to for detailed test results and findings. 
END OF SUMMARY OF FINDINGS AND RECOMMENDATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Page 1 
Hawaii • California 
 GENERAL 
This report presents the results of our geotechnical engineering services 
performed during the test pile program for the Engie Puako Solar Development, located 
in the Puako area in the District of South Kohala on the Island of Hawaii. The project 
location and general vicinity are shown on the Project Location Map, Plate 1. 
In general, this report presents our field observations and the results of testing 
performed on the driven test piles installed and load tested between November 17, 2020 
and January 14, 2021.  The purpose of our geotechnical engineering services was to 
monitor the geotechnical aspects of the test pile installation and testing. 
Project Considerations 
The solar farm development project is located Mauka (east) of Queen Kaahumanu 
Highway in the Puako area on the Island of Hawaii.  The project site encompasses an 
area of over 400 acres.  Based on the information provided, we understand that it is 
desired to develop a solar farm at the subject site. 
Details of the proposed development were not available at the time this report was 
prepared.  However, we envision that a solar array will be constructed at the majority of 
the project site.  We understand wide flange beams (W6x9) are considered for the 
foundation support of the new solar arrays.  Therefore, a test pile program was 
undertaken to support the driven pile foundation design for the solar arrays planned for 
the development. 
As part of the test pile program, a total of 128 test piles were driven to depths of 
about 2 to 7 feet below the existing ground surface. In general, compression, lateral and 
tensile load tests were performed on the driven piles. The approximate test pile locations 
are shown on the Site Plan, Plate 2. 
Purpose and Scope 
The purpose of the pile testing services is to provide pile driving and load testing 
data for the design of the production pile foundation system. The scope of work for this 
test pile program included the following tasks and work efforts:

1. 
Preconstruction activities, including the development of the test pile 
program scope of work and testing procedures, review of test setup and 
procedures, and attendance of coordination meetings.

geologist. 
3.

5.

testing procedures developed by RBI Solar, Inc.

piles. 
8. 
Engineering analyses and interpretation of the compressive, lateral, and 
tensile load test results. 
9.

installation records and results of the load tests performed. 
10. 
Coordination of the overall work on the project by our senior engineer. 
11. 
Quality assurance of the work and consultation by our principal engineer. 
12. 
Miscellaneous work efforts such as drafting, word processing, clerical 
support, and reproduction.

 TEST RESULTS AND DESIGN RECOMMENDATIONS 
The following sections provide detailed discussions of the test pile installation and 
load test results, including discussions and our recommendations for the solar array 
foundations for the project. 
The test piles were installed and load tested by Goodfellow Bros., Inc. (GBI) under 
a subcontract to Geolabs, Inc. using a Vermeer PD-10 pile driver between 
November 17, 2020 and January 14, 2021. The approximate locations of the test piles 
driven are shown on the Site Plan, Plate 2.  In general, the pile driving and load testing 
program was conducted in accordance with the procedures developed by RBI Solar, Inc. 
A summary of the W6X9 wide flange beam physical properties used in the test pile 
program is provided in the table below.

Results of the test pile installation are presented in Appendix A. Results of the 
compressive, lateral, and tensile load tests performed are presented in Appendix B.  
Selected photographs of the pile installation and testing program are presented in 
Appendix C. 
Driven Pile Installation 
A total of 128 W6x9 test piles were installed at the project site. The pile driving 
operations were conducted under the near-continuous observation of our geologist. 
During the pile driving operations, logs were maintained for each test pile to document 
information pertaining to pile number, location, date driven, depth driven, driving time, 
driving rate, and observations made during the pile driving operations. A Summary of 
Driven Piles is provided on Plates A-1.1 through A-1.4. Individual pile driving logs are 
presented in Pile Driving Records, Plates A-2.1 through A-2.128.  
SECTION 2. TEST RESUTS AND DESIGN RECOMMENDATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Page 4 
Hawaii • California 
In general, the initial target pile depth of the piles were about 5 feet below the 
ground surface.  For some piles that did not meet the load testing requirements, additional 
piles were driven with the target depth increased to about 7 feet below the ground surface. 
Some piles encountered refusal conditions during pile driving prior to the test pile 
reaching the target pile depth of about 5 to 7 feet below the ground surface.  Refusal 
conditions were encountered in 28 of the 115 piles driven.  Therefore, additional piles 
were driven into a predrilled hole.  These pile locations were predrilled down to the target 
depth of about 5 feet below the ground surface using an air track drill rig equipped with a 
5- or 6-inch diameter button bit.  Because the air track drill rig displaces soil from the 
drilled hole, a 3/4-inch base course was used to backfill the predrilled hole. The piles were 
driven through the backfilled hole to the target pile depth or until refusal conditions were 
encountered.  
A total of 13 additional pile locations were predrilled and driven.  These driven piles 
(installed in a predrilled hole) are designated as Pile Nos. 8P5, 8P6, 13P5, 18P5, 19P5, 
20P5, 29P5, 42P5, 45P5, 46P5, 62P6, 64P6, and 72P6.  Of the nine piles driven into a 
5-inch diameter predrilled hole (pile number notation XXP5), four piles encountered 
refusal conditions at depths ranging from about 2 to 4.5 feet below the ground surface.  
Of the four piles driven into a 6-inch diameter predrilled hole (pile number notation XXP6), 
one pile encountered refusal condition at about 4.5 feet below the ground surface. 
Driven Pile Load Testing 
Test piles of various driven depths were subjected to compressive, lateral, and 
tensile load tests in general accordance with the testing order and procedures developed 
by RBI Solar, Inc. A Summary of Pile Load Tests is provided on Plates B-1.1 through 
B-1.4. Individual pile load test records are presented in Pile Load Test Records, Plates 
B-2.1 through B-2.234. 
2.2.1 Compressive Load Tests 
In general, compressive load tests were performed by applying a load at the top of 
the pile and measuring the vertical movement of the pile with a dial gauge.  The 
SECTION 2. TEST RESUTS AND DESIGN RECOMMENDATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Page 5 
Hawaii • California 
criterion for passing the compressive load test was defined as less than 0.5 inches 
of movement at 6.5 kips of axial compressive load. 
A total of 112 compressive load tests were conducted on the driven piles.  Only 
one pile, Pile No. 15.1, failed the compressive load test.  Pile No. 15.1 was driven 
to 7 feet below the ground surface.  The remaining 111 compressive load tests all 
met the load test criteria. 
2.2.2 Lateral Load Tests 
Lateral pile load tests were conducted by applying a lateral load at about 4 feet above 
the existing ground surface.  The pile deflection was measured with a dial gauge 
positioned at about 3 inches above the existing ground surface. In general, the test 
piles were laterally loaded to the maximum test load of about 4 kips in approximately 
1-kip load increments. The criterion for passing the lateral load test was defined as 
less than 1 inch of deflection at the 3-kip loading. 
A total of 117 lateral load tests were performed on the driven piles.  One hundred 
twelve out of 117 lateral load tests performed met the testing criteria.  Five piles, 
Pile Nos. 8.1, 18, 29, 42.1, and 64, experienced lateral deflection greater than 
1-inch at 3 kips of lateral load.  It should be noted that the five piles were driven to 
depths ranging from about 2.5 to 3.5 feet below the ground surface and did not 
reach the target embedment depth of 5 feet.  
2.2.3 Tensile Load Tests 
Tensile load tests were conducted by pulling up on the pile using a boot attached to 
near the bottom of the pile.  The upward movement of the pile was measured using 
a dial gauge.  The criterion for passing the tensile load test was defined as less than 
0.5 inches of movement at 7.5 kips of the uplift load. 
A total of 115 tensile load tests were performed on the driven piles.  Twenty-three 
out of 115 tensile load tests performed did not meet the testing criteria.  Of the 
23 failed tensile tests, 20 of the piles were driven to the target embedment depth 
of about 5 feet below the ground surface. 
SECTION 2. TEST RESUTS AND DESIGN RECOMMENDATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Page 6 
Hawaii • California 
Discussion of Pile Driving and Load Testing Results 
Based on the results of the pile testing program, we believe that the installation of 
solar array foundations utilizing W6x9 piles is generally appears feasible at the project 
site.  However, there are some risks and cost impacts that should be taken into 
consideration for the planning and design of the solar farm development. 
In general, the ground surface at the project site consists of dry volcanic ash with 
scattered cobbles and boulders.  An existing unpaved road was utilized to provide access 
to our equipment and personnel.  In addition, new trails were created by leveling the 
ground using a vibratory drum roller.  A backhoe was also used in some areas that 
required additional clearing.  Due to the size of the project, we envision that extensive 
efforts may be required to provide access for equipment and personnel during the 
production pile installation operations.   
Majority of the piles, 87 out of 115, were able to be driven to the design target 
embedment depth of about 5 feet below the ground surface.  However, about 24 percent 
of the piles encountered refusal conditions prior to reaching the target embedment depth.  
Therefore, some pile locations will require predrilling and backfilling with suitable 
materials prior to driving.  Due to the large size and undulating topography of the project 
site, we envision that identifying the locations where piles may encounter refusal would 
be difficult.  Therefore, contingency for predrilling and backfilling should be anticipated 
during the production pile driving. 
Based on the results of the pile load testing, predrilling using a 5-inch diameter bit 
produced more favorable results than using a 6-inch diameter bit for the W6x9 piles.  All 
eight load tests performed on the piles driven into a 5-inch diameter predrilled hole yielded 
passing results for compressive, lateral and tensile load tests.  It should be noted that 
Pile No. 20P5 was not load tested since it encountered refusal condition at about 2 feet 
below the ground surface.  In contrast, only one out of the four load tests performed on 
the piles driven into a 6-inch diameter predrilled hole yielded passing results for 
compressive, lateral and tensile load tests. 
SECTION 2. TEST RESUTS AND DESIGN RECOMMENDATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Page 7 
Hawaii • California 
In general, passing results were obtained for the vast majority of compressive 
(111 out of 112) and lateral (112 out of 117) load tests performed for the project.  
However, about 20 percent of the piles tested (23 out of 115) failed in tension.  Therefore, 
load tests should be performed on production piles to confirm the design load capacities.  
Contingency measures to handle piles that failed the load tests should be developed for 
the production pile installation. 
END OF DISCUSSION AND RECOMMENDATIONS

 LIMITATIONS 
The findings and recommendations presented in this geotechnical engineering 
report are based upon results obtained from the load tests conducted on the test piles 
indicated in this report and our experience in the vicinity. Variations of the subsurface 
conditions between and beyond the test pile locations may occur, and the nature and 
extent of these variations may not become evident until additional field investigation 
and/or construction is underway. 
This geotechnical engineering report has been prepared for the exclusive use of 
Engie Services US and their project consultants for specific application to the solar array 
foundation design of the proposed Engie Puako Solar Development as described herein 
in accordance with generally accepted geotechnical engineering principles and practices. 
No warranty is expressed or implied. 
This report has been prepared solely for the purpose of assisting the design 
engineers for the project planning and design only. Therefore, this report may not contain 
sufficient data, or the proper information, for use to form the basis for preparation of 
construction cost estimates or contract bidding. A contractor wishing to bid on this project 
should retain a competent geotechnical engineer to assist in the interpretation of this 
report and/or performance of site-specific exploration for bid estimating purposes. 
The owner/client should be aware that unanticipated subsurface conditions are 
commonly encountered. Unforeseen subsurface conditions, such as perched 
groundwater, soft deposits, hard layers or cavities, may occur in localized areas and may 
require additional probing or corrections in the field (which may result in construction 
delays) to attain a properly constructed project. Therefore, a sufficient contingency fund 
is recommended to accommodate these possible extra costs. 
END OF LIMITATIONS 
W.O. 8098-10
